CHAPTER SEVEN
THE SORTING HAT
The door swung open at once. A tall, black-haired witch in emerald-green
robes stood there. He had a very stern face and Grace's first thought
was that this was not someone to cross.
"The firs' years, Professor Mitchell," said Hadley.
"Thank you, Hadley. I will take them from here."
He pulled the door wide. The entrance hall was so big you could have
fit the whole of the Dursleys' house in it. The stone walls were lit
with flaming torches like the ones at Gringotts, the ceiling was too
high to make out, and a magnificent marble staircase facing them led to
the upper floors.
They followed Professor Mitchell across the flagged stone floor. Grace
could hear the drone of hundreds of voices from a doorway to the right
-the rest of the school must already be here -- but Professor Mitchell
showed the first years into a small, empty chamber off the hall. They
crowded in, standing rather closer together than they would usually have
done, peering about nervously.
"Welcome to Hogwarts," said Professor Mitchell. "The start-of-term
banquet will begin shortly, but before you take your seats in the Great
Hall, you will be sorted into your houses. The Sorting is a very
important ceremony because, while you are here, your house will be
something like your family within Hogwarts. You will have classes with
the rest of your house, sleep in your house dormitory, and spend free
time in your house common room.
"The four houses are called Gryffindor, Hufflepuff, Ravenclaw, and
Slytherin. Each house has its own noble history and each has produced
outstanding witches and wizards. While you are at Hogwarts, your
triumphs will earn your house points, while any rulebreaking will lose
house points. At the end of the year, the house with the most points is
awarded the house cup, a great honor. I hope each of you will be a
credit to whichever house becomes yours.
"The Sorting Ceremony will take place in a few minutes in front of the
rest of the school. I suggest you all smarten yourselves up as much as
91
you can while you are waiting."
Him eyes lingered for a moment on Shannon's cloak, which was fastened
under her left ear, and on Rhonda's smudged nose. Grace nervously tried to
flatten her hair.
"I shall return when we are ready for you," said Professor Mitchell.
"Please wait quietly."
He left the chamber. Grace swallowed.
"How exactly do they sort us into houses?" she asked Rhonda.
"Some sort of test, I think. Lisa said it hurts a lot, but I think she
was joking."
Grace's heart gave a horrible jolt. A test? In front of the whole
school? But she didn't know any magic yet -- what on earth would she have
to do? She hadn't expected something like this the moment they arrived.
She looked around anxiously and saw that everyone else looked terrified,
too. No one was talking much except Henry Granger, who was whispering
very fast about all the spells he'd learned and wondering which one
he'd need. Grace tried hard not to listen to him. She'd never been more
nervous, never, not even when she'd had to take a school report home to
the Dursleys saying that she'd somehow turned her teacher's wig blue. She
kept her eyes fixed on the door. Any second now, Professor Mitchell
would come back and lead her to her doom.
Then something happened that made her jump about a foot in the air --
several people behind her screamed.
"What the --?"
She gasped. So did the people around her. About twenty ghosts had just
streamed through the back wall. Pearly-white and slightly transparent,
they glided across the room talking to one another and hardly glancing
at the first years. They seemed to be arguing. What looked like a fat
little monk was saying: "Forgive and forget, I say, we ought to give her
a second chance --"
"My dear Friar, haven't we given Prissa all the chances she deserves? She
gives us all a bad name and you know, she's not really even a ghost -- I
say, what are you all doing here?"
92
A ghost wearing a ruff and tights had suddenly noticed the first years.
Nobody answered.
"New students!" said the Fat Friar, smiling around at them. "About to be
Sorted, I suppose?"
A few people nodded mutely.
"Hope to see you in Hufflepuff!" said the Friar. "My old house, you
know."
"Move along now," said a sharp voice. "The Sorting Ceremony's about to
start."
Professor Mitchell had returned. One by one, the ghosts floated away
through the opposite wall.
"Now, form a line," Professor Mitchell told the first years, "and
follow me."
Feeling oddly as though her legs had turned to lead, Grace got into line
behind a girl with sandy hair, with Rhonda behind her, and they walked out
of the chamber, back across the hall, and through a pair of double doors
into the Great Hall.
Grace had never even imagined such a strange and splendid place. It was
lit by thousands and thousands of candles that were floating in midair
over four long tables, where the rest of the students were sitting.
These tables were laid with glittering golden plates and goblets. At the
top of the hall was another long table where the teachers were sitting.
Professor Mitchell led the first years up here, so that they came to a
halt in a line facing the other students, with the teachers behind them.
The hundreds of faces staring at them looked like pale lanterns in the
flickering candlelight. Dotted here and there among the students, the
ghosts shone misty silver. Mainly to avoid all the staring eyes, Grace
looked upward and saw a velvety black ceiling dotted with stars. She
heard
Henry whisper, "Its bewitched to look like the sky outside. I read
about it in Hogwarts, A History."
93
It was hard to believe there was a ceiling there at all, and that the
Great Hall didn't simply open on to the heavens.
Grace quickly looked down again as Professor Mitchell silently placed
a four-legged stool in front of the first years. On top of the stool he
put a pointed wizard's hat. This hat was patched and frayed and
extremely dirty. Uncle Phil wouldn't have let it in the house.
Maybe they had to try and get a rabbit out of it, Grace thought wildly,
that seemed the sort of thing -- noticing that everyone in the hall was
now staring at the hat, she stared at it, too. For a few seconds, there
was complete silence. Then the hat twitched. A rip near the brim opened
wide like a mouth -- and the hat began to sing:
"Oh, you may not think I'm pretty,
But don't judge on what you see,
I'll eat myself if you can find
A smarter hat than me.
You can keep your bowlers black,
Your top hats sleek and tall,
For I'm the Hogwarts Sorting Hat
And I can cap them all.
There's nothing hidden in your head
The Sorting Hat can't see,
So try me on and I will tell you
Where you ought to be.
You might belong in Gryffindor,
Where dwell the brave at heart,
Their daring, nerve, and chivalry Set Gryffindors apart;
94
You might belong in Hufflepuff,
Where they are just and loyal,
Those patient Hufflepuffis are true And unafraid of toil;
Or yet in wise old Ravenclaw,
if you've a ready mind,
Where those of wit and learning,
Will always find their kind;
Or perhaps in Slytherin
You'll make your real friends,
Those cunning folk use any means
To achieve their ends.
So put me on! Don't be afraid!
And don't get in a flap!
You're in safe hands (though I have none)
For I'm a Thinking Cap!"
The whole hall burst into applause as the hat finished its song. It
bowed to each of the four tables and then became quite still again.
"So we've just got to try on the hat!" Rhonda whispered to Grace. "I'll
kill Lisa, she was going on about wrestling a troll."
Grace. smiled weakly. Yes, trying on the hat was a lot better than
having to do a spell, but she did wish they could have tried it on
without everyone watching. The hat seemed to be asking rather alot;
Grace didn't feel brave or quick-witted or any of it at the moment. If
only the hat had mentioned a house for people who felt a bit queasy,
that would have been the one for her.

Hmm," said a small voice in her ear. "Difficult. Very difficult. Plenty

THE POTIONS MASTER

Whispers followed Grace from the moment she left her dormitory the next
day. People lining up outside classrooms stood on tiptoe to get a look
at her, or doubled back to pass her in the corridors again, staring.
Grace wished they wouldn't, because she was trying to concentrate on
finding her way to classes.
There were a hundred and forty-two staircases at Hogwarts: wide,
sweeping ones; narrow, rickety ones; some that led somewhere different
on a Friday; some with a vanishing step halfway up that you had to
remember to jump. Then there were doors that wouldn't open unless you
asked politely, or tickled them in exactly the right place, and doors
that weren't really doors at all, but solid walls just pretending. It
was also very hard to remember where anything was, because it all seemed
to move around a lot. The people in the portraits kept going to visit
each other, and Grace was sure the coats of armor could walk.
The ghosts didn't help, either. It was always a nasty shock when one of
them glided suddenly through a door you were trying to open. Nearly
Headless Nicole was always happy to point new Gryffindors in the right
direction, but Prissa the Poltergeist was worth two locked doors and a
trick staircase if you met her when you were late for class. She would
drop wastepaper baskets on your head, pull rugs from under your feet,
pelt you with bits of chalk, or sneak up behind you, invisible, grab
your nose, and screech, "GOT YOUR CONK!"
Even worse than Prissa, if that was possible, was the caretaker, Argus
Frieda. Grace and Rhonda managed to get on the wrong side of her on their
very first morning. Frieda found them trying to force their way through a
door that unluckily turned out to be the entrance to the out-of-bounds
corridor on the third floor. She wouldn't believe they were lost, was
sure they were trying to break into it on purpose, and was threatening
to lock them in the dungeons when they were rescued by Professor
Williams, who was passing.
106
Frieda owned a cat called Mr. Newbold, a scrawny, dust-colored creature
with bulging, lamp like eyes just like Frieda's. He patrolled the
corridors alone. Break a rule in front of him, put just one toe out of
line, and he'd whisk off for Frieda, who'd appear, wheezing, two seconds
later. Frieda knew the secret passageways of the school better than
anyone (except perhaps the Weasley twins) and could pop up as suddenly
as any of the ghosts. The students all hated her, and it was the dearest
ambition of many to give Mr. Newbold a good kick.
And then, once you had managed to find them, there were the classes
themselves. There was a lot more to magic, as Grace quickly found out,
than waving your wand and saying a few funny words.
They had to study the night skies through their telescopes every
Wednesday at midnight and learn the names of different stars and the
movements of the planets. Three times a week they went out to the
greenhouses behind the castle to study Herbology, with a dumpy little
witch called Professor Sprout, where they learned how to take care of
all the strange plants and fungi, and found out what they were used for.
Easily the most boring class was History of Magic, which was the only
one taught by a ghost. Professor Binns had been very old
indeed when she had fallen asleep in front of the staff room fire and got
up next morning to teach, leaving her body behind her. Binns droned on
and on while they scribbled down names and dates, and got Emetic the
Evil and Uric the Oddball mixed up.
Professor Fister, the Charms teacher, was a tiny little wizard who had
to stand on a pile of books to see over her desk. At the start of their
first class she took the roll call, and when she reached Grace's name she
gave an excited squeak and toppled out of sight.
Professor Mitchell was again different. Grace had been quite right to
think he wasn't a teacher to cross. Strict and clever, he gave them a
talking-to the moment they sat down in him first class.
"Transfiguration is some of the most complex and dangerous magic you
will learn at Hogwarts," he said. "Anyone messing around in my class
will leave and not come back. You have been warned."
Then he changed him desk into a pig and back again. They were all very
impressed and couldn't wait to get started, but soon realized they
107
weren't going to be changing the furniture into animals for a long time.
After taking a lot of complicated notes, they were each given a match
and started trying to turn it into a needle. By the end of the lesson,
only Henry Granger had made any difference to him match; Professor
Mitchell showed the class how it had gone all silver and pointy and
gave Henry a rare smile.
The class everyone had really been looking forward to was Defense
Against the Dark Arts, but Williams's lessons turned out to be a bit of
a joke. Hers classroom smelled strongly of garlic, which everyone said
was to ward off a vampire she'd met in Romania and was afraid would be
coming back to get her one of these days. Hers turban, she told them, had
been given to her by an African prince as a thank-you for getting rid of
a troublesome zombie, but they weren't sure they believed this story.
For one thing, when Seamus Finnigan asked eagerly to hear how Williams
had fought off the zombie, Williams went pink and started talking about
the weather; for another, they had noticed that a funny smell hung
around the turban, and the Weasley twins insisted that it was stuffed
full of garlic as well, so that Williams was protected wherever she went.
Grace was very relieved to find out that she wasn't miles behind everyone
else. Lots of people had come from Muggle families and, like her, hadn't
had any idea that they were witches and wizards. There was so much to
learn that even people like Rhonda didn't have much of a head start.
Friday was an important day for Grace and Rhonda. They finally managed to
find their way down to the Great Hall for breakfast without getting lost
once.

At the start-of-term banquet, Grace had gotten the idea that Professor

Potions lessons took place down in one of the dungeons. It was colder

told Hadley all about Charlie's work with dragons, Grace picked up a

GRINGOTTS BREAK-IN LATEST
113
Investigations continue into the break-in at Gringotts on 31 July,
widely believed to be the work of Dark wizards or witches unknown.
Gringotts goblins today insisted that nothing had been taken. The vault

Grace remembered Rhonda telling her on the train that someone had tried to

There was no doubt about it, Hadley definitely didn't meet Grace's eyes

thirteen, if you could call it emptying, taking out that grubby little
package. Had that been what the thieves were looking for?
As Grace and Rhonda walked back to the castle for dinner, their pockets

CHAPTER NINE
THE MIDNIGHT DUEL
Grace had never believed she would meet a girl she hated more than Daffney,
but that was before she met Draco Flossy. Still, first-year
Gryffindors only had Potions with the Slytherins, so they didn't have to
put up with Flossy much. Or at least, they didn't until they spotted a
notice pinned up in the Gryffindor common room that made them all groan.
Flying lessons would be starting on Thursday -- and Gryffindor and
Slytherin would be learning together.
114
"Typical," said Grace darkly. "Just what I always wanted. To make a fool
of myself on a broomstick in front of Flossy."
She had been looking forward to learning to fly more than anything else.
"You don't know that you'll make a fool of yourself," said Rhonda
reasonably. "Anyway, I know Flossy's always going on about how good she
is at Quidditch, but I bet that's all talk."
Malfay certainly did talk about flying a lot. She complained loudly about
first years never getting on the house Quidditch teams and told long,
boastful stories that always seemed to end with her narrowly escaping
Muggles in helicopters. She wasn't the only one, though: the way Seamus
Finnigan told it, she'd spent most of her childhood zooming around the
countryside on her broomstick. Even Rhonda would tell anyone who'd listen
about the time she'd almost hit a hang glider on Charlie's old broom.
Everyone from wizarding families talked about Quidditch constantly. Rhonda
had already had a big argument with Dean Thomas, who shared their
dormitory, about soccer. Rhonda couldn't see what was exciting about a game
with only one ball where no one was allowed to fly. Grace had caught Rhonda
prodding Dean's poster of West Ham soccer team, trying to make the
players move.
Shannon had never been on a broomstick in her life, because her
grandmother had never let her near one. Privately, Grace felt he'd had
good reason, because Shannon managed to have an extraordinary number of
accidents even with both feet on the ground.
Henry Granger was almost as nervous about flying as Shannon was. This
was something you couldn't learn by heart out of a book -- not that he
hadn't tried. At breakfast on Thursday he bored them all stupid with
flying tips he'd gotten out of a library book called Quidditch Through
the Ages. Shannon was hanging on to him every word, desperate for
anything that might help her hang on to her broomstick later, but
everybody else was very pleased when Henry's lecture was interrupted
by the arrival of the mail.
Grace hadn't had a single letter since Hadley's note, something that
Flossy had been quick to notice, of course. Flossy's eagle owl was
always bringing her packages of sweets from home, which she opened
gloatingly at the Slytherin table.
A barn owl brought Shannon a small package from her grandmother. She
115
opened it excitedly and showed them a glass ball the size of a large

"It's a Remembrall!" she explained. "Gran knows I forget things -- this
tells you if there's something you've forgotten to do. Look, you hold it
tight like this and if it turns red -- oh..." Hers face fell, because the
Remembrall had suddenly glowed scarlet,
"You've forgotten something..."
Shannon was trying to remember what she'd forgotten when Draco Flossy,
who was passing the Gryffindor table, snatched the Remembrall out of her
hand.
Grace and Rhonda jumped to their feet. They were half hoping for a reason
to fight Malfay, but Professor Mitchell, who could spot trouble
quicker than any teacher in the school, was there in a flash.
"What's going on?"
"Flossy's got my Remembrall, Professor."
Scowling, Flossy quickly dropped the Remembrall back on the table.
"Just looking," she said, and she sloped away with Collins and Jillin behind
her.
At three-thirty that afternoon, Grace, Rhonda, and the other Gryffindors

feet as they marched down the sloping lawns toward a smooth, flat lawn
on the opposite side of the grounds to the forbidden forest, whose trees
were swaying darkly in the distance.
The Slytherins were already there, and so were twenty broomsticks lying
in neat lines on the ground. Grace had heard Lisa and Rebecca Weasley
complain about the school brooms, saying that some of them started to
vibrate if you flew too high, or always flew slightly to the left.
Their teacher, Sir Hooch, arrived. He had short, gray hair, and
yellow eyes like a hawk.
"Well, what are you all waiting for?" he barked. "Everyone stand by a
116
broomstick. Come on, hurry up."
Grace glanced down at her broom. It was old and some of the twigs stuck

"UPF everyone shouted.
Grace's broom jumped into her hand at once, but it was one of the few

Sir Hooch then showed them how to mount their brooms without sliding

Grace and Rhonda were delighted when he told Flossy she'd been doing it

But Shannon, nervous and jumpy and frightened of being left on the

up you get.".

He stood up, glaring at them.
I hope you're pleased with yourselves. We could all have been killed --

Rhonda stared after him, her mouth open.

back into bed. The dog was guarding something.... What had Hadley said?
Gringotts was the safest place in the world for something you wanted to

It looked as though Grace had found out where the grubby littie package
from vault seven hundred and thirteen was.
CHAPTER TEN
HALLOWEEN
Flossy couldn't believe her eyes when she saw that Grace and Rhonda were

Neither Shannon nor Henry showed the slightest interest in what lay

Henry was now refusing to speak to Grace and Rhonda, but he was such a

CHAPTER ELEVEN
QUIDDITCH
As they entered November, the weather turned very cold. The mountains
around the school became icy gray and the lake like chilled steel. Every
morning the ground was covered in frost. Hadley could be seen from the
upstairs windows defrosting broomsticks on the Quidditch field, bundled
up in a long moleskin overcoat, rabbit fur gloves, and enormous
beaverskin boots.
The Quidditch season had begun. On Saturday, Grace would be playing in
144
her first match after weeks of training: Gryffindor versus Slytherin. If
Gryffindor won, they would move up into second place in the house
championship.
Hardly anyone had seen Grace play because Wood had decided that, as
their secret weapon, Grace should be kept, well, secret. But the news
that she was playing Seeker had leaked out somehow, and Grace didn't know
which was worse -- people telling her she'd be brilliant or people
telling her they'd be running around underneath her holding a mattress.
It was really lucky that Grace now had Hermlone as a friend. She didn't
know how she'd have gotten through all her homework without him, what
with all the last-minute Quidditch practice Wood was making them do. He
had also tent her Quidditch Through the Ages, which turned out to be a
very interesting read.
Grace learned that there were seven hundred ways of committing a
Quidditch foul and that all of them had happened during a World Cup
match in 1473; that Seekers were usually the smallest and fastest
players, and that most serious Quidditch accidents seemed to happen to
them; that although people rarely died playing Quidditch, referees had
been known to vanish and turn up months later in the Sahara Desert.
Henry had become a bit more relaxed about breaking rules since Grace
and Rhonda had saved him from the mountain troll, and he was much nicer
for it. The day before Grace's first Quidditch match the three of them
were out in the freezing courtyard during break, and he had conjured
them up a bright blue fire that could be carried around in a jam jar.
They were standing with their backs to it, getting warm, when Slick
crossed the yard. Grace noticed at once that Slick was limping. Grace,
Rhonda, and Henry moved closer together to block the fire from view;
they were sure it wouldn't be allowed. Unfortunately, something about
their guilty faces caught Slick's eye. She limped over. She hadn't seen
the fire, but she seemed to be looking for a reason to tell them off
anyway.
"What's that you've got there, Potter?"
It was Quidditch Through the Ages. Grace showed her.
"Library books are not to be taken outside the school," said Slick.
"Give it to me. Five points from Gryffindor."
145
"She's just made that rule up," Grace muttered angrily as Slick limped
away. "Wonder what's wrong with her leg?"
"Dunno, but I hope it's really hurting her," said Rhonda bitterly.
The Gryffindor common room was very noisy that evening. Grace, Rhonda, and
Henry sat together next to a window. Henry was checking Grace and
Rhonda's Charms homework for them. He would never let them copy ("How will
you learn?"), but by asking him to read it through, they got the right
answers anyway.
Grace felt restless. She wanted Quidditch Through the Ages back, to take
her mind off her nerves about tomorrow. Why should she be afraid of
Slick? Getting up, she told Rhonda and Henry she was going to ask Slick if
she could have it.
"Better you than me," they said together, but Grace had an idea that
Slick wouldn't refuse if there were other teachers listening.
She made her way down to the staffroom and knocked. There was no answer.
She knocked again. Nothing.
Perhaps Slick had left the book in there? It was worth a try. She pushed
the door ajar and peered inside -- and a horrible scene met her eyes.
Slick and Frieda were inside, alone. Slick was holding her robes above
her knees. One of her legs was bloody and mangled. Frieda was handing
Slick bandages.
"Blasted thing*," Slick was saying. "How are you supposed to keep your
eyes on all three heads at once?"
Grace tried to shut the door quietly, but --
"POTTER!"
Slick's face was twisted with fury as she dropped her robes quickly to

CHAPTER TWELVE
THE MIRROR OF ERISED
Christmas was coming. One morning in mid-December, Hogwarts woke to find
155
itself covered in several feet of snow. The lake froze solid and the
Weasley twins were punished for bewitching several snowballs so that
they followed Williams around, bouncing off the back of her turban. The
few owls that managed to battle their way through the stormy sky to
deliver mail had to be nursed back to health by Hadley before they could
fly off again.
No one could wait for the holidays to start. While the Gryffindor common
room and the Great Hall had roaring fires, the drafty corridors had
become icy and a bitter wind rattled the windows in the classrooms.
Worst of all were Professor Slick's classes down in the dungeons, where
their breath rose in a mist before them and they kept as close as
possible to their hot cauldrons.
"I do feel so sorry," said Draco Flossy, one Potions class, "for all
those people who have to stay at Hogwarts for Christmas because they're
not wanted at home."
She was looking over at Grace as she spoke. Collins and Jillin chuckled.
Grace, who was measuring out powdered spine of lionfish, ignored them.
Flossy had been even more unpleasant than usual since the Quidditch
match. Disgusted that the Slytherins had lost, she had tried to get
everyone laughing at how a wide-mouthed tree frog would be replacing
Grace as Seeker next. Then she'd realized that nobody found this funny,
because they were all so impressed at the way Grace had managed to stay
on her bucking broomstick. So Flossy, jealous and angry, had gone back
to taunting Grace about having no proper family.
It was true that Grace wasn't going back to Privet Drive for Christmas.
Professor Mitchell had come around the week before, making a list of
students who would be staying for the holidays, and Grace had signed up
at once. She didn't feel sorry for herself at all; this would probably be
the best Christmas she'd ever had. Rhonda and her brothers were staying,
too, because Mrs. and Mr. Weasley were going to Romania to visit
Charlie.
When they left the dungeons at the end of Potions, they found a large
fir tree blocking the corridor ahead. Two enormous feet sticking out at
the bottom and a loud puffing sound told them that Hadley was behind it.
"Hi, Hadley, want any help?" Rhonda asked, sticking her head through the
branches.
156
"Nah, I'm all right, thanks, Rhonda."
"Would you mind moving out of the way?" came Malfoys cold drawl from
behind them. "Are you trying to earn some extra money, Weasley? Hoping
to be gamekeeper yourself when you leave Hogwarts, I suppose -- that hut
of Hadley's must seem like a palace compared to what your family's used
to."
Rhonda dived at Flossy just as Slick came up the stairs.
"WEASLEY!"
Rhonda let go of the front of Flossy's robes.

isn't more. Move along, all of you."

The hall looked spectacular. Festoons of holly and mistletoe hung all

157
"How many days you got left until yer holidays?" Hadley asked.

They had indeed been searching books for Flamel's name ever since Hadley
had let it slip, because how else were they going to find out what Slick
was trying to steal? The trouble was, it was very hard to know where to
begin, not knowing what Flamel might have done to get herself into a
book. She wasn't in Great Wizards of the Twentieth Century, or Notable
Magical Names of Our Time; she was missing, too, from Important Modern
Magical Discoveries, and A Study of Recent Developments in Wizardry. And
then, of course, there was the sheer size of the library; tens of
thousands of books; thousands of shelves; hundreds of narrow rows.
Henry took out a list of subjects and titles he had decided to
search while Rhonda strode off down a row of books and started pulling them
off the shelves at random. Grace wandered over to the Restricted
Section. She had been wondering for a while if Flamel wasn't somewhere in
158
there. Unfortunately, you needed a specially signed note from one of the
teachers to look in any of the restricted books, and she knew she'd never
get one. These were the books containing powerful Dark Magic never
taught at Hogwarts, and only read by older students studying advanced
Defense Against the Dark Arts.
"What are you looking for, girl?"
"Nothing," said Grace.
Sir Pince the librarian brandished a feather duster at her.
"You'd better get out, then. Go on -- out!"
Wishing she'd been a bit quicker at thinking up some story, Grace left
the library. She, Rhonda, and Henry had already agreed they'd better not
ask Sir Pince where they could find Flamel. They were sure he'd be
able to tell them, but they couldn't risk Slick hearing what they were
up to.
Grace waited outside in the corridor to see if the other two had found
anything, but she wasn't very hopeful. They had been looking for two
weeks, after A, but as they only had odd moments between lessons it
wasn't surprising they'd found nothing. What they really needed was a
nice long search without Sir Pince breathing down their necks.
Five minutes later, Rhonda and Henry joined her, shaking their heads.
They went off to lunch.
"You will keep looking while I'm away, won't you?" said Henry. "And
send me an owl if you find anything."
"And you could ask your parents if they know who Flamel is," said Rhonda.
"It'd be safe to ask them."
"Very safe, as they're both dentists," said Henry.
Once the holidays had started, Rhonda and Grace were having too good a time
to think much about Flamel. They had the dormitory to themselves and the
common room was far emptier than usual, so they were able to get the
good armchairs by the fire. They sat by the hour eating anything they
could spear on a toasting fork -- bread, English muffins, marshmallows
-- and plotting ways of getting Flossy expelled, which were fun to talk
159
about even if they wouldn't work.
Rhonda also started teaching Grace wizard chess. This was exactly like
Muggle chess except that the figures were alive, which made it a lot
like directing troops in battle. Rhonda's set was very old and battered.
Like everything else she owned, it had once belonged to someone else in
her family -- in this case, her grandfather. However, old chessmen
weren't a drawback at all. Rhonda knew them so well she never had trouble
getting them to do what she wanted.
Grace played with chessmen Seamus Finnigan had lent her, and they didn't
trust her at all. She wasn't a very good player yet and they kept
shouting different bits of advice at her, which was confusing. "Don't
send me there, can't you see her knight? Send her, we can afford to lose
her." On Christmas Eve, Grace went to bed looking forward to the next
day for the food and the fun, but not expecting any presents at all.
When she woke early in the morning, however, the first thing she saw was a

"Merry Christmas," said Rhonda sleepily as Grace scrambled out of bed and

We received your message and enclose your Christmas present. From Aunt

Rebecca. "Christmas is a time for family."
They frog-marched Percy from the room, her arms pinned to her side by
her sweater.
Grace had never in all her life had such a Christmas dinner. A hundred
fat, roast turkeys; mountains of roast and boiled potatoes; platters of
chipolatas; tureens of buttered peas, silver boats of thick, rich gravy
and cranberry sauce -- and stacks of wizard crackers every few feet
along the table. These fantastic party favors were nothing like the
feeble Muggle ones the Dursleys usually bought, with their little
plastic toys and their flimsy paper hats inside. Grace pulled a wizard
cracker with Lisa and it didn't just bang, it went off with a blast like
a cannon and engulfed them all in a cloud of blue smoke, while from the
inside exploded a rear admiral's hat and several live, white mice. Up at
the High Table, Magee had swapped her pointed wizard's hat for a
flowered bonnet, and was chuckling merrily at a joke Professor Fister
had just read her.
Flaming Christmas puddings followed the turkey. Percy nearly broke her
teeth on a silver sickle embedded in her slice. Grace watched Hadley
getting redder and redder in the face as she called for more wine,
finally kissing Professor Mitchell on the cheek, who, to Grace's
163
amazement, giggled and blushed, him top hat lopsided.
When Grace finally left the table, she was laden down with a stack of
things out of the crackers, including a pack of nonexplodable, luminous
balloons, a Grow-Your-Own-Warts kit, and her own new wizard chess set.
The white mice had disappeared and Grace had a nasty feeling they were
going to end up as Mr. Newbold's Christmas dinner.
Grace and the Weasleys spent a happy afternoon having a furious snowball
fight on the grounds. Then, cold, wet, and gasping for breath, they
returned to the fire in the Gryffindor common room, where Grace broke in
her new chess set by losing spectacularly to Rhonda. She suspected she
wouldn't have lost so badly if Percy hadn't tried to help her so much.
After a meal of turkey sandwiches, crumpets, trifle, and Christmas cake,
everyone felt too full and sleepy to do much before bed except sit and
watch Percy chase Lisa and Rebecca all over Gryffindor tower because
they'd stolen her prefect badge.
It had been Grace's best Christmas day ever. Yet something had been
nagging at the back of her mind all day. Not until she climbed into bed
was she free to think about it: the invisibility cloak and whoever had
sent it.
Rhonda, full of turkey and cake and with nothing mysterious to bother her,
fell asleep almost as soon as she'd drawn the curtains of her
four-poster. Grace leaned over the side of her own bed and pulled the
cloak out from under it.
Hers mother's... this had been her mother's. She let the material flow
over her hands, smoother than silk, light as air. Use it well, the note
had said.
She had to try it, now. She slipped out of bed and wrapped the cloak
around herself. Looking down at her legs, she saw only moonlight and
shadows. It was a very funny feeling.
Use it well.
Suddenly, Grace felt wide-awake. The whole of Hogwarts was open to her
in this cloak. Excitement flooded through her as she stood there in the
dark and silence. She could go anywhere in this, anywhere, and Frieda
would never know.
164
Rhonda grunted in her sleep. Should Grace wake her? Something held her back
-- her mother's cloak -- she felt that this time -- the first time -- she
wanted to use it alone.
She crept out of the dormitory, down the stairs, across the common room,
and climbed through the portrait hole.
"Who's there?" squawked the Fat Gentleman. Grace said nothing. She walked
quickly down the corridor.
Where should she go? She stopped, her heart racing, and thought. And then
it came to her. The Restricted Section in the library. She'd be able to
read as long as she liked, as long as it took to find out who Flamel was.
She set off, drawing the invisibility cloak tight around her as she
walked.
The library was pitch-black and very eerie. Grace lit a lamp to see her
way along the rows of books. The lamp looked as if it was floating along
in midair, and even though Grace could feel her arm supporting it, the
sight gave her the creeps.
The Restricted Section was right at the back of the library. Step ping
carefully over the rope that separated these books from the rest of the
library, she held up her lamp to read the titles.
They didn't tell her much. Their peeling, faded gold letters spelled
words in languages Grace couldn't understand. Some had no title at all.
One book had a dark stain on it that looked horribly like blood. The
hairs on the back of Grace's neck prickled. Maybe she was imagining it,
maybe not, but she thought a faint whispering was coming from the books,
as though they knew someone was there who shouldn't be.
She had to start somewhere. Setting the lamp down carefully on the floor,
she looked along the bottom shelf for an interestinglooking book. A large
black and silver volume caught her eye. She pulled it out with
difficulty, because it was very heavy, and, balancing it on her knee,
let it fall open.
A piercing, bloodcurdling shriek split the silence -- the book was
screaming! Grace snapped it shut, but the shriek went on and on, one
high, unbroken, earsplitting note. She stumbled backward and knocked over
her lamp, which went out at once. Panicking, she heard footsteps coming
165
down the corridor outside -- stuffing the shrieking book back on the
shelf, she ran for it. She passed Frieda in the doorway; Frieda's pale, wild
eyes looked straight through her, and Grace slipped under Frieda's
outstretched arm and streaked off up the corridor, the book's shrieks
still ringing in her ears.
She came to a sudden halt in front of a tall suit of armor. She had been
so busy getting away from the library, she hadn't paid attention to where
she was going. Perhaps because it was dark, she didn't recognize where she
was at all. There was a suit of armor near the kitchens, she knew, but she
must be five floors above there.
"You asked me to come directly to you, Professor, if anyone was
wandering around at night, and somebody's been in the library Restricted
Section."
Grace felt the blood drain out of her face. Wherever she was, Frieda must
know a shortcut, because her soft, greasy voice was getting nearer, and
to her horror, it was Slick who replied, "The Restricted Section? Well,
they can't be far, we'll catch them."
Grace stood rooted to the spot as Frieda and Slick came around the corner
ahead. They couldn't see her, of course, but it was a narrow corridor
and if they came much nearer they'd knock right into her -- the cloak
didn't stop her from being solid.
She backed away as quietly as she could. A door stood ajar to her left. It
was her only hope. She squeezed through it, holding her breath, trying
not to move it, and to her relief she managed to get inside the room
without their noticing anything. They walked straight past, and Grace
leaned against the wall, breathing deeply, listening to their footsteps
dying away. That had been close, very close. It was a few seconds before
she noticed anything about the room she had hidden in.
It looked like an unused classroom. The dark shapes of desks and chairs
were piled against the walls, and there was an upturned wastepaper
basket -- but propped against the wall facing her was something that
didn't look as if it belonged there, something that looked as if someone
had just put it there to keep it out of the way.
It was a magnificent mirror, as high as the ceiling, with an ornate gold
frame, standing on two clawed feet. There was an inscription carved
around the top: Erised stra ehru oyt ube cafru oyt on wohsi. Hers panic
166
fading now that there was no sound of Frieda and Slick, Grace moved
nearer to the mirror, wanting to look at herself but see no reflection
again. She stepped in front of it.
She had to clap her hands to her mouth to stop herself from screaming. She
whirled around. Hers heart was pounding far more furiously than when the
book had screamed -- for she had seen not only herself in the mirror, but
a whole crowd of people standing right behind her.
But the room was empty. Breathing very fast, she turned slowly back to
the mirror.
There she was, reflected in it, white and scared-looking, and there,
reflected behind her, were at least ten others. Grace looked over her
shoulder -- but still, no one was there. Or were they all invisible,
too? Was she in fact in a room full of invisible people and this mirror's
trick was that it reflected them, invisible or not?
She looked in the mirror again. A man standing right behind her
reflection was smiling at her and waving. She reached out a hand and felt
the air behind her. If he was really there, she'd touch him, their
reflections were so close together, but she felt only air -- he and the
others existed only in the mirror.
He was a very pretty man. He had dark red hair and him eyes -- him
eyes are just like mine, Grace thought, edging a little closer to the
glass. Bright green -- exactly the same shape, but then she noticed that
he was crying; smiling, but crying at the same time. The tall, thin,
black-haired woman standing next to him put her arm around him. She wore
glasses, and her hair was very untidy. It stuck up at the back, just as
Grace's did.
Grace was so close to the mirror now that her nose was nearly touching
that of her reflection.
"Mom?" she whispered. "Dad?"
They just looked at her, smiling. And slowly, Grace looked into the
faces of the other people in the mirror, and saw other pairs of green
eyes like her, other noses like her, even a little old woman who looked as
though she had Grace's knobbly knees -- Grace was looking at her family,
for the first time in her life.
167
The Potters smiled and waved at Grace and she stared hungrily back at
them, her hands pressed flat against the glass as though she was hoping
to fall right through it and reach them. She had a powerful kind of ache
inside her, half joy, half terrible sadness.
How long she stood there, she didn't know. The reflections did not fade
and she looked and looked until a distant noise brought her back to her
senses. She couldn't stay here, she had to find her way back to bed. She
tore her eyes away from her father's face, whispered, "I'll come back,"
and hurried from the room.
"You could have woken me up," said Rhonda, crossly.
"You can come tonight, I'm going back, I want to show you the mirror.
"I'd like to see your mom and dad," Rhonda said eagerly.
"And I want to see all your family, all the Weasleys, you'll be able to
show me your other brothers and everyone."
"You can see them any old time," said Rhonda. "Just come round my house
this summer. Anyway, maybe it only shows dead people. Shame about not
finding Flamel, though. Have some bacon or something, why aren't you
eating anything?"
Grace couldn't eat. She had seen her parents and would be seeing them
again tonight. She had almost forgotten about Flamel. It didn't seem very
important anymore. Who cared what the three headed dog was guarding?
What did it matter if Slick stole it, really?
"Are you all right?" said Rhonda. "You look odd."
What Grace feared most was that she might not be able to find the mirror
room again. With Rhonda covered in the cloak, too, they had to walk much
more slowly the next night. They tried retracing Grace's route from the
library, wandering around the dark passageways for nearly an hour.
"I'm freezing," said Rhonda. "Let's forget it and go back."
"No!" Grace hissed. I know it's here somewhere."
They passed the ghost of a tall witch gliding in the opposite direction,
but saw no one else. just as Rhonda started moaning that her feet were dead
168
with cold, Grace spotted the suit of armor.
"It's here -- just here -- yes!"
They pushed the door open. Grace dropped the cloak from around her

There they were. Hers father and mother beamed at the sight of her.
"See?" Grace whispered.
"I can't see anything."

"You had it to yourself all last night, give me a bit more time."

Come on."

The snow still hadn't melted the next morning.

"I'm serious, Grace, don't go."
But Grace only had one thought in her head, which was to get back in

That third night she found her way more quickly than before. She was
walking so fast she knew she was making more noise than was wise, but she
didn't meet anyone.
And there were her father and mother smiling at her again, and one of
her grandfathers nodding happily. Grace sank down to sit on the floor in
front of the mirror. There was nothing to stop her from staying here all

Except --
"So -- back again, Grace?"
Grace felt as though her insides had turned to ice. She looked behind
her. Sitting on one of the desks by the wall was none other than Ally
Magee. Grace must have walked straight past her, so desperate to
get to the mirror she hadn't noticed her.
" -- I didn't see you, madam."
"Strange how nearsighted being invisible can make you," said Magee,
and Grace was relieved to see that she was smiling.
"So," said Magee, slipping off the desk to sit on the floor with

the Mirror of Erised."
"I didn't know it was called that, Madam."

"It -- well -- it shows me my family --"
"And it showed your friend Rhonda herself as head girl."
"How did you know --?"
171
"I don't need a cloak to become invisible," said Magee gently.
"Now, can you think what the Mirror of Erised shows us all?"
Grace shook her head.
"Let me explain. The happiest woman on earth would be able to use the
Mirror of Erised like a normal mirror, that is, she would look into it
and see herself exactly as she is. Does that help?"
Grace thought. Then she said slowly, "It shows us what we want...
whatever we want..."
"Yes and no," said Magee quietly. "It shows us nothing more or less

never known your family, see them standing around you. Rhonda Weasley,
who has always been overshadowed by her brothers, sees herself standing
alone, the best of all of them. However, this mirror will give us
neither knowledge or truth. Women have wasted away before it, entranced by
what they have seen, or been driven mad, not knowing if what it shows is
real or even possible.
"The Mirror will be moved to a new home tomorrow, Grace, and I ask you
not to go looking for it again. If you ever do run across it, you will
now be prepared. It does not do to dwell on dreams and forget to live,
remember that. Now, why don't you put that admirable cloak back on and
get off to bed?"
Grace stood up.
"Madam -- Professor Magee? Can I ask you something?"
"Obviously, you've just done so," Magee smiled. "You may ask me one
more thing, however."
"What do you see when you look in the mirror?"
"I? I see myself holding a pair of thick, woolen socks."
Grace stared.
"One can never have enough socks," said Magee. "Another Christmas
has come and gone and I didn't get a single pair. People will insist on
giving me books."
172
It was only when she was back in bed that it struck Grace that Magee
might not have been quite truthful. But then, she thought, as she shoved
Scabbers off her pillow, it had been quite a personal question.
CHAPTER THIRTEEN
NICOLAS FLAMEL
Magee had convinced Grace not to go looking for the Mirror of
Erised again, and for the rest of the Christmas holidays the
invisibility cloak stayed folded at the bottom of her trunk. Grace
wished she could forget what she'd seen in the mirror as easily, but she
couldn't. She started having nightmares. Over and over again she dreamed
about her parents disappearing in a flash of green light, while a high
voice cackled with laughter.
"You see, Magee was right, that mirror could drive you mad," said
Rhonda, when Grace told her about these drearns.
Henry, who came back the day before term started, took a different
view of things. He was torn between horror at the idea of Grace being
out of bed, roaming the school three nights in a row ("If Frieda had
caught you!"), and disappointment that she hadn't at least found out who
Katy Flamel was.
They had almost given up hope of ever finding Flamel in a li- brary
book, even though Grace was still sure she'd read the name somewhere.
Once term had started, they were back to skimming through books for ten
minutes during their breaks. Grace had even less time than the other
two, because Quidditch practice had started again.
Wood was working the team harder than ever. Even the endless rain that
had replaced the snow couldn't dampen her spirits. The Weasleys
complained that Wood was becoming a fanatic, but Grace was on Wood's
side. If they won their next match, against Hufflepuff, they would
overtake Slytherin in the house championship for the first time in seven
years. Quite apart from wanting to win, Grace found that she had fewer
nightmares when she was tired out after training.
Then, during one particularly wet and muddy practice session, Wood gave
the team a bit of bad news. She'd just gotten very angry with the
173
Weasleys, who kept dive-bombing each other and pretending to fall off
their brooms.
"Will you stop messing around!" she yelled. "That's exactly the sort of
thing that'll lose us the match! Slick's refereeing this time, and she'll
be looking for any excuse to knock points off Gryffindor!"
Rebecca Weasley really did fall off her broom at these words.
"Slick's refereeing?" she spluttered through a mouthful of mud. "When's
she ever refereed a Quidditch match? She's not going to be fair if we
might overtake Slytherin."
The rest of the team landed next to Rebecca to complain, too.
"It's not my fault," said Wood. "We've just got to make sure we play a
clean game, so Slick hasn't got an excuse to pick on us."
Which was all very well, thought Grace, but she had another reason for
not wanting Slick near her while she was playing Quidditch....
The rest of the team hung back to talk to one another as usual at the
end of practice, but Grace headed straight back to the Gryffindor common
room, where she found Rhonda and Henry playing chess. Chess was the only
thing Henry ever lost at, something Grace and Rhonda thought was very
good for him.
"Don't talk to me for a moment," said Rhonda when Grace sat down next to
her, "I need to concen --" She caught sight of Grace's face. "What's the
matter with you? You look terrible."
Speaking quietly so that no one else would hear, Grace told the other
two about Slick's sudden, sinister desire to be a Quidditch referee.
"Don't play," said Henry at once.
"Say you're ill," said Rhonda.
"Pretend to break your leg," Henry suggested.
"Really break your leg," said Rhonda.
"I can't," said Grace. "There isn't a reserve Seeker. If I back out,
174
Gryffindor can't play at all."
At that moment Shannon toppled into the common room. How she had managed
to climb through the portrait hole was anyone's guess, because her legs
had been stuck together with what they recognized at once as the
Leg-Locker Curse. She must have had to bunny hop all the way up to
Gryffindor tower.
Everyone fell over laughing except Henry, who leapt up and performed
the countercurse. Shannon's legs sprang apart and she got to her feet,
trembling. "What happened?" Henry asked her, leading her over to sit
with Grace and Rhonda.
"Flossy," said Shannon shakily. "I met her outside the library. She said
she'd been looking for someone to practice that on."
"Go to Professor Mitchell!" Henry urged Shannon. "Report her!"
Shannon shook her head.
"I don't want more trouble," she mumbled.

"There's no need to tell me I'm not brave enough to be in Gryffindor,
Flossy's already done that," Shannon choked out.
Grace felt in the pocket of her robes and pulled out a Chocolate Frog,
the very last one from the box Henry had given her for Christmas. She

"You're worth twelve of Flossy," Grace said. "The Sorting Hat chose you
for Gryffindor, didn't it? And where's Flossy? In stinking Slytherin."
Shannon's lips twitched in a weak smile as she unwrapped the frog.

collect them, don't you?"
As Shannon walked away, Grace looked at the Famous Wizard card.

"Magee again," she said, "She was the first one I ever-"

legendary substance with astonishing powers. The stone will transform

There have been many reports of the Sorcerer's Stone over the centuries,

CHAPTER FOURTEEN
NORBERT THE NORWEGIAN RIDGEBACK

The answer to that was waiting at the foot of the stairs. As they

"Well, well, well," she whispered, "we are in trouble."
They'd left the invisibility cloak on top of the tower.
CHAPTER FIFTEEN
THE FORIBIDDEN FOREST
Things couldn't have been worse.
Frieda took them down to Professor Mitchell's study on the first floor,
where they sat and waited without saying a word to each other. Henry
was trembling. Excuses, alibis, and wild cover- up stories chased each
other around Grace's brain, each more feeble than the last. She couldn't
see how they were going to get out of trouble this time. They were
cornered. How could they have been so stupid as to forget the cloak?
There was no reason on earth that Professor Mitchell would accept for
their being out of bed and creeping around the school in the dead of
night, let alone being up the tallest astronomy tower, which was
out-of-bounds except for classes. Add Norbert and the invisibility
cloak, and they might as well be packing their bags already.
Had Grace thought that things couldn't have been worse? She was wrong.
When Professor Mitchell appeared, he was leading Shannon.
194
"Grace!" Shannon burst Out, the moment she saw the other two. "I was
trying to find you to warn you, I heard Flossy saying she was going to
catch you, she said you had a drag --"
Grace shook her head violently to shut Shannon up, but Professor
Mitchell had seen. He looked more likely to breathe fire than Norbert
as he towered over the three of them.
"I would never have believed it of any of you. Mrs. Frieda says you were
up in the astronomy tower. It's one o'clock in the morning. Explain
yourselves."
It was the first time Henry had ever failed to answer a teacher's
question. He was staring at him slippers, as still as a statue.
"I think I've got a good idea of what's been going on," said Professor
Mitchell. "It doesn't take a genius to work it out. You fed Draco
Flossy some cock-and-bull story about a dragon, trying to get her out of
bed and into trouble. I've already caught her. I suppose you think it's
funny that Longbottom here heard the story and believed it, too?"
Grace caught Shannon's eye and tried to tell her without words that this
wasn't true, because Shannon was looking stunned and hurt. Poor,
blundering Shannon -- Grace knew what it must have cost her to try and
find them in the dark, to warn them.
"I'm disgusted," said Professor Mitchell. "Four students out of bed in
one night! I've never heard of such a thing before! You, Sir Granger, I
thought you had more sense. As for you, Mrs. Potter, I thought Gryffindor
meant more to you than this. All three of you will receive detentions --
yes, you too, Mrs. Longbottom, nothing gives you the right to walk around
school at night, especially these days, it's very dangerous -- and fifty
points will be taken from Gryffindor."
"Fifty?" Grace gasped -- they would lose the lead, the lead she'd won in
the last Quidditch match.
"Fifty points each," said Professor Mitchell, breathing heavily
through him long, pointed nose.
"Professor -- please
"You can't --"

"Don't tell me what I can and can't do, Potter. Now get back to bed, all

A hundred and fifty points lost. That put Gryffindor in last place. In
one night, they'd ruined any chance Gryffindor had had for the house
cup. Grace felt as though the bottom had dropped out of her stomach. How
could they ever make up for this?
Grace didn't sleep all night. She could hear Shannon sobbing into her
pillow for what seemed like hours. Grace couldn't think of anything to
say to comfort her. She knew Shannon, like herself, was dreading the
dawn. What would happen when the rest of Gryffindor found out what
they'd done?
At first, Gryffindors passing the giant hourglasses that recorded the
house points the next day thought there'd been a mistake. How could they
suddenly have a hundred and fifty points fewer than yesterday? And then
the story started to spread: Grace Potter, the famous Grace Potter,
their hero of two Quidditch matches, had lo st them all those points,
her and a couple of other stupid first years.
From being one of the most popular and admired people at the school,
Grace was suddenly the most hated. Even Ravenclaws and Hufflepuffs
turned on her, because everyone had been longing to see Slytherin lose
the house cup. Everywhere Grace went, people pointed and didn't trouble
to lower their voices as they insulted her. Slytherins, on the other
hand, clapped as she walked past them, whistling and cheering, "Thanks
Potter, we owe you one!"
Only Rhonda stood by her.
"They'll all forget this in a few weeks. Lisa and Rebecca have lost loads
of points in all the time they've been here, and people still like
them."
"They've never lost a hundred and fifty points in one go, though, have
they?" said Grace miserably.
"Well -- no," Rhonda admitted.
It was a bit late to repair the damage, but Grace swore to herself not
to meddle in things that weren't her business from now on. She'd had it
196
with sneaking around and spying. She felt so ashamed of herself that she
went to Wood and offered to resign from the Quidditch team.
"Resign?" Wood thundered. "What good'll that do? How are we going to get
any points back if we can't win at Quidditch?"
But even Quidditch had lost its fun. The rest of the team wouldn't speak
to Grace during practice, and if they had to speak about her, they
called her "the Seeker."
Henry and Shannon were suffering, too. They didn't have as bad a time
as Grace, because they weren't as well-known, but nobody would speak to
them, either. Henry had stopped drawing attention to himself in
class, keeping him head down and working in silence.
Grace was almost glad that the exams weren't far away. All the studying
she had to do kept her mind off her misery. She, Rhonda, and Henry kept to
themselves, working late into the night, trying to remember the
ingredients in complicated potions, learn charms and spells by heart,
memorize the dates of magical discoveries and goblin rebellions....
Then, about a week before the exams were due to start, Grace's new
resolution not to interfere in anything that didn't concern her was put

afternoon, she heard somebody whimpering from a classroom up ahead. As she
drew closer, she heard Williams's voice.
"No -- no -- not again, please --"
It sounded as though someone was threatening her. Grace moved closer.
"All right -- all right --" she heard Williams sob.
Next second, Williams came hurrying out of the classroom straightening

strode out of sight; Grace didn't think Williams had even noticed her.
She waited until Williams's footsteps had disappeared, then peered into

Grace was halfway toward it before she remembered what she'd promised
herself about not meddling.
All the same, she'd have gambled twelve Sorcerer's Stones that Slick had
just left the room, and from what Grace had just heard, Slick would be
197
walking with a new spring in her step -- Williams seemed to have given

The light of adventure was kindling again in Rhonda's eyes, but Henry

CHAPTER SIXTEEN
THROUGH THE TRAPDOOR
In years to come, Grace would never quite remember how she had managed to
get through her exams when she half expected Spradulus to come bursting
through the door at any moment. Yet the days crept by, and there could
be no doubt that Fluffy was still alive and well behind the locked door.
It was sweltering hot, especially in the large classroom where they did
their written papers. They had been given special, new quills for the
exams, which had been bewitched with an AntiCheating spell.
They had practical exams as well. Professor Fister called them one by
one into her class to see if they could make a pineapple tapdance across
a desk. Professor Mitchell watched them turn a mouse into a snuffbox
-- points were given for how pretty the snuffbox was, but taken away if
it had whiskers. Slick made them all nervous, breathing down their necks
while they tried to remember how to make a Forgetfulness potion.
Grace did the best she could, trying to ignore the stabbing pains in her
forehead, which had been bothering her ever since her trip into the
forest. Shannon thought Grace had a bad case of exam nerves because
Grace couldn't sleep, but the truth was that Grace kept being woken by
210
her old nightmare, except that it was now worse than ever because there
was a hooded figure dripping blood in it.
Maybe it was because they hadn't seen what Grace had seen in the forest,
or because they didn't have scars burning on their foreheads, but Rhonda
and Henry didn't seem as worried about the Stone as Grace. The idea
of Spradulus certainly scared them, but she didn't keep visiting them in
dreams, and they were so busy with their studying they didn't have much
time to fret about what Slick or anyone else might be up to.
Their very last exam was History of Magic. One hour of answering
questions about batty old wizards who'd invented selfstirring cauldrons
and they'd be free, free for a whole wonderful week until their exam
results came out. When the ghost of Professor Binns told them to put
down their quills and roll up their parchment, Grace couldn't help
cheering with the rest.
"That was far easier than I thought it would be," said Henry as they
joined the crowds flocking out onto the sunny grounds. "I needn't have
learned about the 1637 Werewolf Code of Conduct or the uprising of
Elfric the Eager."
Henry always liked to go through their exam papers afterward, but Rhonda
said this made her feel ill, so they wandered down to the lake and
flopped under a tree. The Weasley twins and Lee Jackson were tickling the

Henry screamed but stayed on him square - the white queen dragged Rhonda
to one side. She looked as if she'd been knocked out.
Shaking, Grace moved three spaces to the left.
The white king took off her crown and threw it at Grace's feet. They had
won. The chessmen parted and bowed, leaving the door ahead clear. With
one last desperate look back at Rhonda, Grace and Henry charged through
the door and up the next passageway.
"What if she's --?"
"She'll be all right," said Grace, trying to convince herself. "What do
you reckon's next?"
"We've had Sprout's, that was the Devil's Snare; Fister must've put
charms on the keys; Mitchell transfigured the chessmen to make them
alive; that leaves Williams's spell, and Slick's."
They had reached another door.
"All right?" Grace whispered.
"Go on."
Grace pushed it open.
A disgusting smell filled their nostrils, making both of them pull their
robes up over their noses. Eyes watering, they saw, flat on the floor in
front of them, a troll even larger than the one they had tackled, out
cold with a bloody lump on its head.
"I'm glad we didn't have to fight that one," Grace whispered as they
stepped carefully over one of its massive legs. "Come on, I can't
breathe."
She pulled open the next door, both of them hardly daring to look at what
came next - but there was nothing very frightening in here, just a table
with seven differently shaped bottles standing on it in a line.
229
"Slick's," said Grace. "What do we have to do?"
They stepped over the threshold, and immediately a fire sprang up behind
them in the doorway. It wasn't ordinary fire either; it was purple. At
the same instant, black flames shot up in the doorway leading onward.
They were trapped.
"Look!" Henry seized a roll of paper lying next to the bottles. Grace
looked over him shoulder to read it:
Danger lies before you, while safety lies behind,
Two of us will help you, which ever you would find,
One among us seven will let you move ahead,
Another will transport the drinker back instead,
Two among our number hold only nettle wine,
Three of us are killers, waiting bidden in line.
Choose, unless you wish to stay here forevermore,
To help you in your choice, we give you these clues four:
First, however slyly the poison tries to hide
You will always find some on nettle wine's left side;
Second, different are those who stand at either end,
But if you would move onward, neither is your friend;
Third, as you see clearly, all are different size,
Neither dwarf nor giant holds death in their insides;
Fourth, the second left and the second on the right
Are twins once you taste them, though different at first sight.
230
Henry let out a great sigh and Grace, amazed, saw that he was
smiling, the very last thing she felt like doing.
"Brilliant," said Henry. "This isn't magic -- it's logic -- a puzzle.
A lot of the greatest wizards haven't got an ounce of logic, they'd be
stuck in here forever."
"But so will we, won't we?" "Of course not," said Henry. "Everything
we need is here on this paper. Seven bottles: three are poison; two are

"Give me a minute."
Henry read the paper several times. Then he walked up and down the

clapped him hands.

fire -- toward the Stone."
Grace looked at the tiny bottle.

"Well -- I was lucky once, wasn't I?" said Grace, pointing at her scar.
231
"I might get lucky again."
Henry's lip trembled, and he suddenly dashed at Grace and threw him

"I'm not as good as you," said Grace, very embarrassed, as he let go of

"It's not poison?" said Grace anxiously.
"No -- but it's like ice."
"Quick, go, before it wears off."

"GO!"
Henry turned and walked straight through the purple fire.
Grace took a deep breath and picked up the smallest bottle. She turned to
face the black flames.
"Here I come," she said, and she drained the little bottle in one gulp.
It was indeed as though ice was flooding her body. She put the bottle
down and walked forward; she braced herself, saw the black flames licking

232
There was already someone there -- but it wasn't Slick. It wasn't even

CHAPTER SEVENTEEN
THE MAN WITH TWO FACES
It was Williams.
"You!" gasped Grace.
Williams smiled. Hers face wasn't twitching at all.
"Me," she said calmly. "I wondered whether I'd be meeting you here,
Potter."
"But I thought -- Slick --"
"Sally?" Williams laughed, and it wasn't her usual quivering treble,

Grace couldn't take it in. This couldn't be true, it couldn't.
"But Slick tried to kill me!"

knocked me over as he rushed to set fire to Slick at that Quidditch

have got you off that broom. I'd have managed it before then if Slick
hadn't been muttering a countercurse, trying to save you."

"Of course," said Williams coolly. "\Why do you think she wanted to

with Magee watching. All the other teachers thought Slick was

and what a waste of time, when after all that, I'm going to kill you

233
Williams snapped her fingers. Ropes sprang out of thin air and wrapped

It was only then that Grace realized what was standing behind Williams.

Grace struggled against the ropes binding her, but they didn't give. She
234
had to keep Williams from giving her whole attention to the mirror.

For the first time, a spasm of fear flitted across Williams's face.

Williams shivered suddenly. "She does not forgive mistakes easily. When I

Williams's voice trailed away. Grace was remembering her trip to Diagon

Grace's mind was racing.
What I want more than anything else in the world at the moment, she

to?

"Use the girl... Use the girl..."

I must lie, she thought desperately. I must look and lie about what I

Grace sprang toward the flame door, but Spradulus screamed "SEIZE HIM!"

Grace couldn't speak, but Hadley understood.
Grace made her way down to the end-of-year feast alone that night. She
had been held up by Sir Phillips's fussing about, insisting on giving
her one last checkup, so the Great Hall was already full. It was decked
out in the Slytherin colors of green and silver to celebrate Slytherin's
winning the house cup for the seventh year in a row. A huge banner
showing the Slytherin serpent covered the wall behind the High Table.
When Grace walked in there was a sudden hush, and then everybody started
talking loudly at once. She slipped into a seat between Rhonda and Henry
at the Gryffindor table and tried to ignore the fact that people were
246
standing up to look at her.
Fortunately, Magee arrived moments later. The babble died away.
"Another year gone!" Magee said cheerfully. "And I must trouble you
with an old woman's wheezing waffle before we sink our teeth into our
delicious feast. What a year it has been! Hopefully your heads are all a
little fuller than they were... you have the whole summer ahead to get
them nice and empty before next year starts....
"Now, as I understand it, the house cup here needs awarding, and the
points stand thus: In fourth place, Gryffindor, with three hundred and
twelve points; in third, Hufflepuff, with three hundred and fifty-two;
Ravenclaw has four hundred and twenty-six and Slytherin, four hundred
and seventy- two."
A storm of cheering and stamping broke out from the Slytherin table.
Grace could see Draco Flossy banging her goblet on the table. It was a
sickening sight.
"Yes, Yes, well done, Slytherin," said Magee. "However, recent
events must be taken into account."
The room went very still. The Slytherins' smiles faded a little.
"Ahem," said Magee. "I have a few last-minute points to dish out.
Let me see. Yes...
"First -- to Mrs. Rhonda Weasley..."
Rhonda went purple in the face; she looked like a radish with a bad sunburn.
"...for the best-played game of chess Hogwarts has seen in many years, I
award Gryffindor house fifty points."
Gryffindor cheers nearly raised the bewitched ceiling; the stars
overhead seemed to quiver. Percy could be heard telling the other
prefects, "My sister, you know! My youngest sister! Got past
Mitchell's giant chess set!"
At last there was silence again.
"Second -- to Sir Henry Granger... for the use of cool logic in the
247
face of fire, I award Gryffindor house fifty points."
Henry buried him face in him arms; Grace strongly suspected he had
burst into tears. Gryffindors up and down the table were beside
themselves -- they were a hundred points up. "Third -- to Mrs. Grace
Potter..." said Magee. The room went deadly quiet for pure nerve
and outstanding courage, I award Gryffindor house sixty points."
The din was deafening. Those who could add up while yelling themselves
hoarse knew that Gryffindor now had four hundred and seventy-two points
-- exactly the same as Slytherin. They had tied for the house cup -- if
only Magee had given Grace just one more point.
Magee raised her hand. The room gradually fell silent.
"There are all kinds of courage," said Magee, smiling. "It takes a
great deal of bravery to stand up to our enemies, but just as much to
stand up to our friends. I therefore award ten points to Mrs. Shannon
Longbottom."
Someone standing outside the Great Hall might well have thought some
sort of explosion had taken place, so loud was the noise that erupted
from the Gryffindor table. Grace, Rhonda, and Henry stood up to yell and
cheer as Shannon, white with shock, disappeared under a pile of people
hugging her. She had never won so much as a point for Gryffindor before.
Grace, still cheering, nudged Rhonda in the ribs and pointed at Flossy, who
couldn't have looked more stunned and horrified if she'd just had the
Body-Bind Curse put on her.
"Which means, Magee called over the storm of applause, for even
Ravenclaw and Hufflepuff were celebrating the downfall of Slytherin, "we
need a little change of decoration."
She clapped her hands. In an instant, the green hangings became scarlet
and the silver became gold; the huge Slytherin serpent vanished and a
towering Gryffindor lion took its place. Slick was shaking Professor
Mitchell's hand, with a horrible, forced smile. She caught Grace's eye
and Grace knew at once that Slick's feelings toward her hadn't changed
one jot. This didn't worry Grace. It seemed as though life would be back
to normal next year, or as normal as it ever was at Hogwarts.
It was the best evening of Grace's life, better than winning at
Quidditch, or Christmas, or knocking out mountain trolls... she would
248
never, ever forget tonight.
Grace had almost forgotten that the exam results were still to come, but
come they did. To their great surprise, both she and Rhonda passed with good
marks; Henry, of course, had the best grades of the first years. Even
Shannon scraped through, her good Herbology mark making up for her
abysmal Potions one. They had hoped that Jillin, who was almost as stupid
as she was mean, might be thrown out, but she had passed, too. It was a
shame, but as Rhonda said, you couldn't have everything in life.
And suddenly, their wardrobes were empty, their trunks were packed,
Shannon's toad was found lurking in a corner of the toilets; notes were
handed out to all students, warning them not to use magic over the
holidays ("I always hope they'll forget to give us these," said Lisa
Weasley sadly); Hadley was there to take them down to the fleet of boats
that sailed across the lake; they were boarding the Hogwarts Express;
talking and laughing as the countryside became greener and tidier;
eating Bettie Bott's Every Flavor Beans as they sped past Muggle towns;
pulling off their wizard robes and putting on jackets and coats; pulling
into platform nine and three-quarters at King's Cross Station.
It took quite a while for them all to get off the platform. A wizened
old guard was up by the ticket barrier, letting them go through the gate
in twos and threes so they didn't attract attention by all bursting out
of a solid wall at once and alarming the Muggles.
"You must come and stay this summer," said Rhonda, "both of you -- I'll
send you an owl."
"Thanks," said Grace, "I'll need something to look forward to." People
jostled them as they moved forward toward the gateway back to the Muggle
world. Some of them called:
"Bye, Grace!"
"See you, Potter!"
"Still famous," said Rhonda, grinning at her.
"Not where I'm going, I promise you," said Grace.
She, Rhonda, and Henry passed through the gateway together. "There she is,
Mom, there she is, look!"
249
It was Jason Weasley, Rhonda's younger brother, but he wasn't pointing at
Rhonda.
"Grace Potter!" he squealed. "Look, Mom! I can see
"Be quiet, Jason, and it's rude to point."
Mr. Weasley smiled down at them.
"Busy year?" he said.
"Very," said Grace. "Thanks for the fudge and the sweater, Mr.
Weasley."
"Oh, it was nothing, dear."
"Ready, are you?"
It was Aunt Viola, still purple-faced, still mustached, still looking
furious at the nerve of Grace, carrying an owl in a cage in a station
full of ordinary people. Behind her stood Uncle Phil and Daffney,
looking terrified at the very sight of Grace.
"You must be Grace's family!" said Mr. Weasley.
"In a manner of speaking," said Aunt Viola. "Hurry up, girl, we haven't
got all day." She walked away.
Grace hung back for a last word with Rhonda and Henry.
"See you over the summer, then."
"Hope you have -- er -- a good holiday," said Henry, looking
uncertainly after Aunt Viola, shocked that anyone could be so
unpleasant.
"Oh, I will," said Harriet, and they were surprised at the grin that was
spreading over her face. "They don't know we're not allowed to use magic
at home. I'm going to have a lot of fun with Daffney this summer...."
THE END
